=041  \\$ager
=100  \\$aMüller, Heinrich$d1631-1675$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q69725$4aut$96872
=245  \\$aEvangelischer Herzens-Spiegel
=260  \\$aRatzeburg$bHoffmann$c1697
=300  \\$a[xviii-838-[2]- pages$bleather bound, metal locks, marbled edges, Title page in red and black ink, engraved double frontispiece, front papers are detached, notes in ink on various endpapers
=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1679
=500  \\$aReform theologian Heinrich Müller was a German devotional author, Protestant writer of hymns, a Lutheran minister and theologian and a professor at the University of Rostock from 1647 to 1650. He famously denounced the font, the pulpit, the confessional, and the altar as "the four dumb idols of the Lutheran Church".  Müller attempted to address the faithful convincingly through word and writing and also tried to renew the spiritual life against the internal resistance of the church. As a reform theologian, he opposed a Christianity that was fixated purely on outward appearances. He left behind numerous manuscripts, of which the "Evangelische Herzensspiegel", which was published after his death; most of his writings were burnt in 1677.
=500  \\$avery thick volume with metal locks
=500  \\$aSeveral front- and backpapers contain manuscript notes (german, black ink) with diary entries and listings of names for the period of 1708 until 1720
=500  \\$afront cover embossed text "Wolmar von Scheydingh 1704"
=500  \\$aDouble frontispiece engraving with view of Lübeck,  biblical scenes and portraits of the author Heinrich Müller and Joachim Lütkemann 
=501  \\$aBound in with 'Apostolische Aüffmünterüng zum lebendigen Glauben in Christo Jesu'
=561  \\$aEx libris Wolmar von Scheydingh (embossed on front cover)
=590  \\$aErklärung der Sonntäglichen und fürnehmsten Fest-Evangelien vorgestellet, wie auch D. Joachimi Lutkemanni Erklärung der Sonn- und Festtages Episteln durchs gantze Jahr, mit beijgefügten Passion-Predigten. Nebst einer Vorrede. D. Augist. Pfeiffers der Lübischen Kirchen Superintendens.

=041  \\$ager
=100  \\$aSlevogt, Gottlieb$dabout 1694-1732$4aut$97457
=245  \\$aGründliche Untersuchung von denen Rechten der Altäre, Tauf-Steine, Beicht-Stühle, Predigt-Stühle, Kirch-Stunde, Gottes-Künsten, Orgeln, Kirchen-Musik, Glocken, Thürmer und Gottes-Aecker$baus dem Canonischen und Protestantischen Kirchen-Recht erläutert
=260  \\$aJena$bRitter$c1732
=300  \\$a[xxxii]-517-[7] pages$bfrontispiece black & red, illustration, leather cover
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aSlevogt was born at the end of the 17th century (details conspicuously unknown) in Jena, where he studied, received his doctorate in 1716 and devoted himself to the practice of law. He died in February 1732 as a ducal Altenburg court and government advocate and imperial comes palatinus, but left behind a heavy burden of debt, so that his family declined completely. Slevogt's writings belong mainly to Protestant canon law, which they treat sometimes historically-archaeologically, sometimes practically. His German work on the law of the altars combines both points of view with a mildly reasonable appreciation and toleration of all ceremonial activity.

=500  \\$aGaius Lucilius (c. 180-103/2 BC) was the earliest Roman satirist, of whose writings only fragments remain. A Roman citizen of the equestrian class, he was born at Suessa Aurunca in Campania, and was a member of the Scipionic Circle.
=500  \\$aHe may be called the inventor of poetical satire, as he was the first to impress upon the rude inartistic medley, known to the Romans by the name of satura, that character of aggressive and censorious criticism of persons, morals, manners, politics, literature, etc. which the word satire has ever since denoted.

=245  \\$aNeujahrsgeschenke ab der Chorherren
=260  \\$aZürich$bChorherrensaal$c1779-1818; 1819-36
=300  \\$a2 vols. ([i]-8-8-11-[ii]-10-8-[ii]-10-[ii]-8-[ii]-8-[ii]-8-[ii]-8-[ii]-8-[ii]-8-[ii]-8-[ii]-8-[ii]-8-[ii]-12îi]-8-[ii]-8-[vi]-12-[ii]-12-[ii]-12-[ii]-11-[ii]-15-[ii]-16-[ii]-15-[ii]-8-[ii]-11-[iv]-5-[ii]-7-[ii]-8-[ii]-16-[ii]-8-[ii]-7-[ii]-14-[ii]-14-[ii]-10-[ii]-15-[ii]-12-[ii]-10 + [ii]-48-[32]-[ii]-40-[ii]-7-[ii]-15-[ii]-11-[ii]-39-[ii]-14-[ii]-12-[ii]-18-]ii]-9-[ii]-8-[ii]-11-[ii]-15-[ii]-7-[ii]-24-[ii]-8-[ii]-11-[ii]-20 pages)$billustrations, plates, portraits, marbled carboard cover, leather spine embossed in gold & red
=500  \\$aMainly biographical stories with a moral and religious exemplary function that glorify Swiss national history, Swiss history of the Reformation, etc., each one preceded by a full-page engraving illustrating the content of the story, or portraying the person whose life is described.
=500  \\$aThe editions, published every New year as a speech for the pupils of the Collegium, have no specific title. Some exeptions hint in the title to its content, eg. 1819 "...zum Andenken der im Jahre 1519 begonnenen Glaubenverbesserung "
=500  \\$aPortraits (and biographies) of:
Ulrich Zwingli (1484-1531)
Johan Heinrich Lavater 
Ludwig Lavater (1527-1586)
Heinrich Corrodi 1752-1793

Josua Mahler (1529-1598)
Salomon Schinz M.D. (1734-1784)
Johann Jacob Scheuchzer (1672-1733)

=500  \\$a“In the 17th century music in Zürich was dominated by three collegia musica: the first was ‘zum Chorherrensaal’, followed by the ‘ab dem Musiksaal’ (from 1613) and ‘zur deutschen Schule’ (from 1679). Initially they were concerned only with sacred music, but later also performed contemporary German and Italian secular music. The three societies merged in 1812 to form the Allgemeine Musikgesellschaft Zürich (AMGZ), which since 1813 has produced books on musical subjects in a series of ‘Neujahrsblättern’, the successors to a series of New Year collections of polyphonic pieces published by two of the collegia musica from 1685 and 1713 respectively.”

=500  \\$a'Excess and Avarice', although it appeared as play number 32 in 1714, was one of the first plays Van Halmael wrote. In the preface, he himself calls it "a flower plucked in my youth" dating it thus in the latter half of the 17th century. It contains within it a small opera ('Opera, or singing tragedy of Pyramus and Thisbe') composed by Servaes de Koninck (original music lost?) a Flemish baroque composer of motets, Dutch songs, chamber and incidental music, French airs and Italian cantatas. After training and starting his career in Flanders de Koninck moved to Amsterdam, where he was active in circles connected to the Amsterdam Theatre

=300  \\$a4 vols. in 1 ([x]-320-448-[7] pages)$bleather bound, engraved frontispiece, illustrations
=500  \\$aCollected work of Jan Harmenszoon Krul 
=500  \\$aKrul was a Dutch song poet, playwright, ironmonger and bookseller.His portrait was painted in 1633 by Rembrandt. He founded the Amsterdamsche Musijck Kamer, devoted to the cultivation of music drama. Krul wrote successful pastoral, erotic, love poems and Catholic, religious poetry for bigots. Krul argued for a harmonious combination of music and rhetoric and introduced a different poetic style from Vondel, less sumptuous, rather naive. His language is simple, fluent, direct. Shepherd life is staged in half of his plays.

=534  \\$cKempten: Dreher, 1673
=585  \\$aDisplayed as part of the 'Musica ex Machina' exhibition at EPFL Pavilions, Lausanne, 20 September 2024-29 June 2025
=590  \\$aOder mechanische Geheim-Verbindung der Kunst und Natur, durch Stimme und Hall-Wissenschaft gestifftet, worinn ingemein der Stimm, Thons, Hall- und Schalles Natur, Eigenschafft, Krafft und Wunder-Würckung, auch deren geheime Ursachen, mit vielen neu- und ungemeinen Kunst-Wercken und Proben vorgestellet werden. Ingleichem wie die Sprach- und Gehör-Instrumenta, Machinen und Kunst-Wercke, vorbildender Natur, zur Nach-Ahmung, so wohl die Stimm, Hall und Schall, an weit-entlegene Ort zu führen, als auch in abgesonderten Geheim-Zimmern, auff kunst-verborgene Weise, vertreulich und ungefähr sich mit-einander zu unterreden, sollen verfertigt werden. =100  \\$aBeckmann, Johann Christoph$d1641-1717$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q105443$97617
=245  \\$aAccessiones historiæ Anhaltinæ$bVon unterschiedenen Das Hoch-Fürstl. Hauß Und Fürstenthum Anhalt Belangenden Materien sampt dazu gehörigen Documenten
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aZerbst$bZimmermann$c1716
=300  \\$a[vi]-632-[7] pages$bplates, folded pages
=500  \\$aBeckmann was a German university professor, librarian and historian. He taught Greek, history, politics and theology at the Brandenburg University of Frankfurt and was the university's rector for many years. Bekmann published numerous works in various fields. His alphabetical catalogue of the Frankfurt University Library, published in 1676, which was an innovation at the time, became significant. He also earned lasting merit as a chronicler of the Anhaltinian principalities and the Mark Brandenburg.

=500  \\$aIn part 2 (p. 225 etc): musical notation and information on plainchant.
=520  \\$aAntoine de Montazet (17 August 1713-2 May 1788) was a French theologian, of Jansenist tendencies, who became bishop of Autun and archbishop of Lyon. He was elected to the Académie française in 1756. Contrary to the papal bull of Pope Pius V on the Roman Breviary, Montazet changed the text of the Breviary and the Missal. The later efforts of Pope Pius IX and Cardinal Bonald to suppress the innovations of Montazet provoked resistance on the part of the canons, who defended the traditional Lyonnese ceremonies (Wikipedia).

=500  \\$aProtestantism in Strasbourg is an important aspect of the history and sociology of the city. The Protestant Reformation was introduced in Strasbourg as early as 1518, when Matthieu Zell preached in Strasbourg in the Lutheran manner. In 1520, Pierre-Philippe de Remiremont preached the Reformation in the church of Saint-Pierre-le-Vieux in Strasbourg. In 1524, the pastor Martin Bucer moved to the church of Sainte-Aurélie in Strasbourg, outside the walls of Old Strasbourg, and then 1531 to the church of Saint Thomas in Strasbourg. In 1529 the cathedral was given over to Protestant worship. The city officially joined Lutheranism in 1532.

=500  \\$aJohann Lauremberg, also Johannes Lauremberg, occasionally incorrect: Johann Wilhelm Laurenberg (* 26 February 1590 in Rostock; † 28 February 1658 in Sorø, Denmark) was a mathematician and cartographer as well as a Low German poet and writer of the Baroque period. As a pseudonym he used the name "Hans Willmsen L. Rost." (= Johann, son of Wilhelm Lauremberg Rostochiensis).

=500  \\$aA novena (from Latin: novem, "nine") is an ancient tradition of devotional praying in Christianity, consisting of private or public prayers repeated for nine successive days or weeks. The prayers are often derived from devotional prayer books, or consist of the recitation of the rosary (a "rosary novena"), or of short prayers through the day. Novena prayers are customarily printed in small booklets, and the novena is often dedicated to a specific angel, saint, Marian title of the Blessed Virgin Mary, or one of the persons of the Holy Trinity.
=500  \\$aAs the author Fr. Bernardo de Santa Maria Rosa was preacher and Master of Ceremonies of the Royal Convent of S. Francisco da Cidade do Porto, it could well be that this prayer/songbook was used at the Novenas for the Virgin in the liturgic rituals at the abbey mentioned. The feast day of the Virgin of the Immaculate Conception is 8 December.
=500  \\$aEngraved Frontispiece, iconography of the Virgin of the Immaculate Conception shows her standing, with arms outstretched or hands clasped in prayer.

=500  \\$aAntoine de Pas, Marquis de Feuquières (1648 - 1711) was a French writer and soldier, who served in the wars of Louis XIV. His "Mémoires de M. le Marquis de Feuquiere, lieutenant general des armées du roi: contenans les maximes sur la guerre, & l'application des exemples aux maximes" ran to 42 editions between 1736 and 2014 and was translated into three languages. Completed just before his death in 1711, it was highly critical of Louis XIV and remained unpublished until 1736. Voltaire later used it as a source for his own work, "Siècle de Louis XIV". 
=500  \\$a The book begins with a long biographical presentation of the marquis written by the abbot Gabriel Pérau to whom  we owe this edition. 
=500  \\$aParticularly comprehensive, it includes a good understanding of the importance that France had in the Thirty Years' War and the particularly fundamental role of the Marquis de Feuquières in the formation of the alliance against the House of Austria.

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aJoly, Claude$d1607-1700$4aut$97709
=245  \\$aRecueil de maximes véritables et importantes pour l'institution du Roy
=260  \\$aParis$bElsevier$c1653
=300  \\$a[xxii]-584-[2] pages$bgilded pages
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aThe most prominent rebellions in the mid-seventeenth century France were those of the nobles and the judges and known as the 'Fronde'.The leading theoretician of the parleamentary fronde was Claude Joly. His treatise 'Recueil de maximes' is a collection of constitutionalist maxims, remnants of a pre-absolutist age, and include trenchant attacks on two contributions of Cardinals Richelieu and Mazarin to political thought and practice in France. One was the new motion that the king is rightly the master - in effect the owner - of the persons and properties of all inhabitants of France. The other was the Machiavellian view that succesful public policy requires the systematic use of immoral means. The King's power, warned Joly, is limited and not automatically sanctionned by divine law. Frenchmen posess just title to their lives and properties, and are not the slaves of a despot or tyrant. The king's original divine power is mediated through the French people, Joly added, and the king cannot rightfully tax the French without the consent of the states-general. The fact that Joly was reviled by the king and his party as a rebel and a traitor, he declared, shows that the old constitutionhas been overcome by new views holding the king to have unlimited authority above all law. For Joly this view was 'pure usurpation'  bred in the 'monstrous cauldron' of Machiavel.

=500  \\$aCharles Rollin (1661-1741) was a French historian and educator, very popular in his time. His literary work dates chiefly from the later years of his life, when he had been forbidden to teach. His once famous Ancient History (French: Histoire Ancienne, 12 vols., Paris, 1730–38) and the less generally read Roman History (Histoire Romaine, only five of nine volumes finished by the time of his death) were avowed compilations, uncritical and somewhat inaccurate. But they instructed and interested, generation after generation.

=500  \\$aVerdussen was a dynasty of printers in Antwerp, starting with Hieronymus Verdussen I in the late sixteenth century, and ending around 1800. Many other printers in Antwerp were also related to the Verdussens through marriage. They specialized in religious works and works in Spanish,[1] but also published newspapers, almanachs, poetry, scientific works, .... By the end of the 17th century, they produced about 21% of the Spanish books printed in the Netherlands, and with 5 presses was second only to Moretus in Antwerp.

=100  \\$aBoer, Francijntje de$d1784-1852$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2299757$97737
=245  \\$aNieuwe dichtproeven$bvan Francijntje De Boer Dienstmaagd te Sneek

=300  \\$a[xxii]-75-[1] pages$bclippings
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aContains some loose clippings - papercraft and illustrations from printed sources - as well as a handwritten leaflet notificating the death of Francijntje de Boer
=500  \\$aFrancijntje de Boer was a Dutch maid and writer of particularly successful children's poems. Between 1815 and 1825, she published four volumes of poetry, three of which were for children. Her language is characterised by simplicity. Her poems revolve around domesticity, virtue and pure religiousness. Despite her modest social position, she had contact with other Dutch female poets, including Fenna Mastenbroek, Petronella Moens and Anna Barbara van Meerten-Schilperoort. During her lifetime, she enjoyed widespread fame. A total of eight editions of her 'Gedichtjes voor kinderen' appeared until the end of 1870, and a French translation by Auguste Clavareau in 1835. The various printings varied in design and illustration, and were widely distributed, serving in schools as prizes for pupils or as teaching material.

=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1616
=500  \\$aLucelle is a true Romeo & Juliet adaptation by Bredero. A play that moved Maria Tesselschade to tears at the premiere in 1615, a play that was immortalised many times by painters such as Jan Steen and Jan Miense Moleaer, a play that was reprinted more than any of Bredero's plays in the 17th and 18th centuries, a play with the recognisable topical emotion of unattainable love due to a difference in descent.

=041  \\$adut
=245  \\$aEpitaphium, ofte graf-dicht op 't overlyden vanden sinrijcken Poeets G. A. Brederode
=260  \\$as.l.$bs.n.$cs.d.
=300  \\$a[14] pages
=500  \\$aElegies after the death of Bredero. 
=500  \\$aDigitized later edition at https://www.dbnl.org/tekst/stui002memo01_01/stui002memo01_01_0041.php
=500  \\$aOriginal title page (with portrait of Bredero) is missing (cut out?)
=500  \\$aThis edition of Elegies (Lijck-dichten) shows clearly the status of Bredero as a local celebrity at that very moment. Such a publication was unprecedented, and it demonstrates how popular the poet was among his fellow citizens. They all strongly and intensely experienced the loss. The elegies were written by different poets, including famous Dutch authors like Samuel Coster, Petrus Scriverius and Joost van den Vondel. It marks Bredero’s decease as a moment at which Amsterdam authors sing the praises of their popular and much-loved former colleague. The poems predominantly breathe the usual funeral topics of praise, grief and consolation. But the very first of all these poems, a lengthy `Epitaph, or elegy on the death of the significant poet G.A. Bredero’ (`Epitaphium. Oft Graf-dicht Op ’t overlyden vanden sinrijcken Poeet G.A. Brederood’), tells its readers how Bredero died a sudden death, (probably heart failure).

=500  \\$aKöhler was a German historian, numismatist and heraldist. He served as university librarian at Altdorf (Nürnberg) and contributed substantially to early library science. The 1728 'Sylloge' is one of three monographs upon which Köhler's credentials as a library and information scientist are based upon. Though compiling older texts by Jean Garnier, Frederik Rostgaard, Giusto Fontanini, and Daniel Wilhelm Moller, it can be seen as one of the first anthologies of library classification, organization and cataloguing schemes.

=500  \\$aLuigi Antonio Sabbatini (1732-1809) was an Italian composer and music theorist. He studied music at Bologna in the Franciscan Monastery, under Father Giovanni Battista Martini. He published a textbook on the theoretical elements of music, in 1789, in three volumes, a treatise on fugues, in 1802. He also contributed to the use of numerical signatures of musical harmony. In May 1807, he was elected to the Accademia Italiana.

=245  \\$aWerkstäte der heutigen Künste oder Die neue Kunsthistorie$nvol. 6
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aBrandenburg$aLeipzig$bHalle$c1779
=300  \\$a[193] pages$b6 folded, illustrated sheets inserted
=500  \\$aContains only pages page 215-408: the "Nachtrag zum Orgelbauer"
=500  \\$aHalle studied theology, philosophy and mathematics in Königsberg. In 1753, after completing his studies, he came to Berlin as an educator. There he was appointed to the Royal Prussian Cadet Corps (Corps des Cadets) in 1760 to take over the newly established professorship for history. He was the author of various scientific, technical/technological and historical (educational) books.

In his six-volume Werkstäte der heutigen Künste oder die neue Kunsthistorie, Halle describes the crafts of his time in great detail.

=100  \\$aSerre, Jean Adam$d1704-1788$4aut$97860
=245  \\$aEssais sur les principes de l'harmonie
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bPrault$c1753
=300  \\$a[viii]-206 pages
=500  \\$aPublished during the Querelle des Bouffons by a painter, physicist, chemist and musical theorist whom Burney met in Geneva
=500  \\$aSerre studied painting at the academy of Geneva, and at the university, after studying natural sciences, defended a thesis in physics under the direction of Jean-Louis Calandrini. He worked as a miniaturist in Marseille, Vienna and Paris, where he settled in 1751. He published several articles in the Mercure de France which he reused in his Essais sur les principes de l'harmonie in 1753, entering into debate with Charles-Henri Blainville, Rameau and Leonhard Euler. In 1756, he stayed in London and returned to Geneva where he published his Observations sur les principes de l'harmonie [...] in 1763: he challenged the musical theories developed by d'Alembert in the article "Fondamental" in the Encyclopédie, the 'Trattato di musica secondo la vera scienza dell'armonia' by Giuseppe Tartini and the 'Dictionaire harmonique' by Francesco Geminiani.
=500  \\$aIt was translated and commented on in German by Johann Adam Hiller in 1767 and quoted several times in Jean-Jacques Rousseau's Dictionnaire de musique.

=500  \\$aTitle-page engraving by Daniel Chodowiecki  (1726-1801), German-Polish painter and printmaker. Allegory of the fine arts: the picture shows a light female figure surrounded by Minerva and the Graces. Minerva sits with lance and medusa shield. At her feet are tools for carving stone, a palette, brush, compass and square, masks and cothurn, a shawm and a plectrum. Minerva looks up at the female figure standing next to her, her gaze directed into the distance as if listening to an inner voice. A bright sun shines above the standing one. Minerva points with her hand to the instruments on the floor which refer to the three fine arts of painting, sculpture and architecture as well as to poetry and music.the three graces, meanwhile, are busy endowing the standing female figure with attributes that point to various arts. In the background, a landscape opens up in the depths, in which a naked, still uncivilised human family sits in front of a kind of primitive hut while one of them chases a deer. (Veronika Mertens, Die drei Grazien, Studien zu einem Bildmotiv in der Kunst der Neuzeit, Harrassowitz Verlag, 1994)

=501  \\$aRedenvoering voor de comedie
Noodig verweer-schrift voor den Nederduitschen Kerken-raadt van Utrecht
Wederlegging van het zoogenaamde verweerschrift voor de Nederduitze Kerkenraad van Utrecht en het kortbondig vertoog van de onbetamelykheid en schadelykheid der comedien
Bekentmaking van het roekeloos bestaan van Pieter Burman, vermaart Professor in de Akademie van Utrecht
Antwoord van A. J. Brakonier, C. Boott, Ae. vande Putt, en A. Driessen, predikanten te Utrecht, op Profr. Pieter Burmans zoogenaamde wederlegginge van 't noodig verweerschrift
Tweede wederlegginge van het antwoord van de vier Utrechtze predikanten vol. 1
Tweede wederlegginge der vier Utrechtse predikanten vols. 2-3
De gehoonde eer van God den hoogsten wetgever, en Zyn oppergebied over de koninkryken en staten van de wereld
Ad mirmillones sine missione depugnantes
Advertissement of Waarschouwinge aan alle liefhebbers van den waren Christelyken Godtsdienst, aangaande den rechten toestant der vermaadre Akademie van Utrecht

=500  \\$a2 remarkable engravings included: title page (elaborate printers-logo) and first page (town-view of the Voorhout square in The Hague).
=501  \\$aBound in with 'Kerkuraia mastix' and 'Groete aen de ioffrouwen'
=520  \\$aThe title of this great work of poetry, 'Batava Tempe', an ode to a beautiful and famous street in the old city centre of The Hague, the Lange Voorhout, accurately conveys the content. The word Tempe is derived from a beautiful valley in northern Greece, Thessaly to be precise, which was so called in antiquity. Apparently Huygens relates this beautiful valley to the Voorhout in The Hague. So the poem is about the Voorhout, which is also called Batave Tempe and is located in The Hague. Constantijn Huygens could also have chosen another place to write a great poem about, but apparently the Voorhout surpassed all other places and played the most important role for him in his life.

=041  \\$alat
=100  \\$aZehentner, Paul$d1589-1648$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q55874362$97979
=245  \\$aPromontorium malæ spei: impiis periculose navigantibus propositum
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aHaupt; Widmanstadt$bGraz$c1643
=300  \\$a[xxxviii]-752-[10] pages$bgilt edges, 2 engravings
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aJesuit warning of the consequences of licentiousness ("Promontory, thoughts of hope for the wicked goal that sailed dangerously. Whether it is a sign of rejection and note: procrastination of repentance written precautionary men's amendment is reluctance, sometimes hope to repent.")
=500  \\$aFirst and only edition of a Latin edifying text on moral and religious issues by the Jesuit Paul Zehentner (1589-1648), preacher at the Graz court of the widow of the Holy Roman Emperor Ferdinand II and teacher of grammar, the humanities and the Holy Scripture at Millestadt in Austria. A moral-theological treatment of state theory, astrology and magic, intended to highlight the dangers of licentious behaviour. 
=500  \\$aIt provides our first known reference to the tragedy of Leontius, a play Zehentner saw at the Jesuit University in Ingolstadt in 1615, and which was to serve as a prototype for the Don Juan legend (Keefe, Mozart studies, p. 140). 
=500  \\$aZehentner dedicated the book to Leonardus Helfridus, Count at Maggau, 26 October 1643, and received a privilege from the Holy Roman Emperor Ferdinand III.
=500  \\$aEngraved allegorical frontispiece and a richly designed armorial and emblematic dedication plate, both by David Tscherning.
=504  \\$aindex

=500  \\$aIn 1822 Logier was called to Berlin to help found a music academy, and subsequently trained elementary teachers on behalf of the king until 1826. =110  \\$4edt$aAllgemeine Musikgesellschaft Zürich (Switzerland)$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2648827$921129
=245  \\$aMusicalische Neu-Jahrs-Gedichte von der Music-Gesellschaft auf der Teutschen Schul in Zürich
=260  \\$aZürich$bDeutsche Schule$c1714-40
=300  \\$a224 pages$bmusic, illustrations
=500  \\$aIn the 17th century music in Zürich was dominated by three collegia musica: the first was ‘zum Chorherrensaal’, followed by the ‘ab dem Musiksaal’ (from 1613) and ‘zur deutschen Schule’ (from 1679). Initially they were concerned only with sacred music, but later also performed contemporary German and Italian secular music. The three societies merged in 1812 to form the Allgemeine Musikgesellschaft Zürich (AMGZ), which since 1813 has produced books on musical subjects in a series of ‘Neujahrsblättern’, the successors to a series of New Year collections of polyphonic pieces published by two of the collegia musica from 1685 and 1713 respectively.
=500  \\$aSee 04J20, 04J21, 10B20, 11H13, G1-027 and G1-028 for similar collections
=500  \\$aEach year between 1713 and 1740 has a New Year's poem and a song with an engraved frontispiece (‘Kupfer-Blatt') bound in, numbered I-XXVIII, but paginated continuously
=500  \\$aThe poems and plates deal predominantly with music, e.g. Jubal's invention of music
=500  \\$aMost songs have Cantus I and Bassus on left page, Cantus II and Altus on right page, but some are for two sopranos only, whose parts face each other; still others have a basso continuo (bassus generalis) part for 'organum'

=245  \\$aMusicalische Neu-Jahrs-Gedichte $nvol. 1/7
=260  \\$aZürich$bMusiksaal$c1716-50
=300  \\$a528 pages$bcardboard bound, red edges, engraved title page, music examples, 66 plates, some fold-outs
=500  \\$aCompilation of 'Neu-Jahrsblättern' from 1685-1750, numbered continuously and hence reprinted
=500  \\$a“In the 17th century music in Zürich was dominated by three collegia musica: the first was ‘zum Chorherrensaal’, followed by the ‘ab dem Musiksaal’ (from 1613) and ‘zur deutschen Schule’ (from 1679). Initially they were concerned only with sacred music, but later also performed contemporary German and Italian secular music. The three societies merged in 1812 to form the Allgemeine Musikgesellschaft Zürich (AMGZ), which since 1813 has produced books on musical subjects in a series of ‘Neujahrsblättern’, the successors to a series of New Year collections of polyphonic pieces published by two of the collegia musica from 1685 and 1713 respectively.”
=500  \\$asee 04J20, 04J21, 10B20, 11H13, G1-027 and G1-028 for similar collections
=500  \\$aeach year has an emblematic plate (some depicting musical elements, such as tempi, dynamics  and mythical musicians, others showing sights from Zürich, and yet others featuring musical iconography), followed by a poem, a strophic song and sometimes psalms and/or quotes from the Bible or from writings by Seneca, Breitinger, Saavedra, Augustine, Kircher, Ovid
=500  \\$apages 272-280 offers a cantata entitled "Schall und Wiederhall der Freyjahrs Posaunen, daß Zions Sternen Kranz bekommen neuen Glanz, oder Herzerfreuliche Wiedergedächtnuß des Freyjahrs der Kirchen Christi, welches durch den himlicherleuchteten Werkzeugen der Ehr und Lehr Gottes Hrn. M. Hudrich Zwinglein, gebührtig in dem Wilden Hause bey St. Johann im Togganburg: henach getreueifrigen Antistitem der lieben Kirchen Zürich, und hochverdienten Hrn. Reformatorem, zur seligen Glaubens-Verbesserung den 1. Tag Jenner im 1519. Jahr Christi glücklich wieder eingeführet, und nun den 1. Tag Jenner des 1719. Jahrs Christi bey einer Kunst- und Tugendliebenden Jugend loblicher Statt Zürich erneueret ware: als dero ein würdiges Lobopfer in den Mund legen wöllen eine ehren-Gesellschaft auf dem neuerbauten Music-Saal"
=500  \\$ap. 315 contains a pencil notation, indicating that the "Herrn Burgermeister" is Joh. Heinr. Herzel, elect. A. 1723
=500  \\$aone plate, no. LIV (interleaves between pages 424 and 425), is offered in three versions
=590  \\$aGott zu ehren und zu Vermehrung der Freuden in Gott einer Ehr- Kunst-und Tugend-liebenden Jugend in Zürich Von der Gesellschaft der Vocal- und Instrumental-Music, ab dem Music-Sal daselbst zum anderen mahl aufgelegt.

=500  \\$aAmbrosius Lobwasser was a German humanist and translator, born in Saxony. He is best known for this Psalter des Königlichen Propheten David , published in 1573 (Leipzig). This metrical psalter, a translation of the French Genevan psalter by Clément Marot and Théodore de Bèze, became one of the standard psalm-books used by the evangelical churches of the German-speaking lands, including Switzerland. The Lobwasser psalter was widely reprinted into the 1800s.

=260  \\$aHamburg$bBohn$c1771
=300  \\$a3 vols. in 1 (xxviii-130-[2]+178-[10]+xxii-180-[2] pages)$bfrontispiece engraving, engraved title page
=500  \\$aHagedorn incorporated ancient, French and above all English inspirations into cheerful, sensible fables and tales (1738) and anacreontic, dallying odes and songs (1742-1752). Formally, his works can be divided into fables, songs, didactic poems and epigrams. His poetry is kept simple (alternating verse, easily singable stanzaic forms) and pursues different stylistic ideals than the poets of the Baroque. 
=500  \\$aMozart set his poem Die Alte (The Old Woman) in his song of the same name (K. 517) in 1787. Joseph Haydn set two of his poems in his canons (a capella songs) (Hob. XXVIIb).

=100  \\$aPinot Duclos, Charles$d1704-1772$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q982034$98370
=245  \\$aHistoire de Madame De Luz;  anecdotte du règne d'Henri IV
=260  \\$aThe Hague$bHondt, de$c1741
=300  \\$a426-22 pages$btitle page in red and black ink
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aThrough a vivid portrait of a woman of sovereign innocence, Duclos denounces the hypocrisy of a prudish society. Madame de Luz is a sort of libertine Princess of Cleves, a moralist's novel that is also a praise of femininity.
=504  \\$aMadame de Luz is one of the most beautiful women in the kingdom of Henry IV, virtuous and loyal to her husband. She is secretly in love with the Marquis de Saint-Geran, but tries to forget this passion.

Her husband, the Baron de Luz, is involved in a plot led by the Maréchal de Biron, Governor of Burgundy, to overthrow Henry IV. Arrested, the Baron de Luz is threatened with the death penalty. Convinced of his innocence and determined to free him, Madame de Luz intervenes with one of the judges at the trial, Monsieur de Thurin, a suitor whom she had once spurned. Thurin is ready to clear the Baron's name if she accepts his advances. Madame de Luz resists and then gives in to the blackmail. Her life then turns upside down. She has committed a sin from which she will never recover.

=500  \\$aFirst edition of this curious and unusual work, in which the author, physician to the polish King Stanislas (Stanisław I Leszczyński 1677-1766) seeks to study the "influence of the passions" on the development of diseases: this is one of the first treatises on the subject, which was very popular at the end of the 18th and beginning of the 19th centuries. =500  \\$aHenri Pène du Bois, an American writer, literary critic, and journalist whose friendship with French author Guy de Maupassant (1850-1893) was the source of his son’s name. Born in a cultured, sophisticated family of French origin but with roots in America dating back to 1748, he was an avowed francophile and created a sophisticated environment deeply engaged in the French culture. He accompanied his son Guy, a painter, on a trip to Paris in 1905. His tragic death in 1906 on board of the ship for their return home to America forced Guy to turn to art criticism to help support his family.

=500  \\$aDes Maizeaux translated the works of Charles de Saint-Évremond in English from the French published in 1714 during his exile in England. The book also described the author's life, a translation from his "La Vie de St Evremond", published in 1711.
=500  \\$aCharles de Marguetel de Saint-Denis, seigneur de Saint-Évremond, was a French soldier, hedonist, essayist and literary critic. After 1661, he lived in exile, mainly in England, as a consequence of his attack on French policy. He wrote for his friends and did not intend his work to be published, although a few of his pieces were leaked in his lifetime. The first full collection of his works was published in London in 1705, after his death.

=100  \\$aVilliers, Pierre de$d1648-1728$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2820887$98511
=245  \\$aLes Mémoires de la vie du Comte D***, avant sa retraite
=260  \\$as.l.$bs.n.$c1740
=300  \\$a2 vols. ([vi]-xxxii-352 + [iv]-xxxii-371 pages)$btitle page in red and black ink, engraved frontispiece in vol.1, engraved title pages
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$a"Mr L'Abbé de Villiers, si connu par son Art de prêcher, & par plusieurs autres Ouvrages, qui ont eu l'aprobation du public" (in Oeuvres de Monsieur de Saint Evremond, I,  p.296)
=500  \\$aDe Villiers wrote many works in the seventeenth century, and many biographies and studies are attributed to him, such as Lettres sur l'oraison des quiétistes or Prière en vers sur l'espérance qu'on doit avoir en Jésus-Christ.He  was the first to suspect that Perrault's tales were not written by Charles Perrault's son, as announced by the publishers, but by the academician himself - or at least at second hand. De Villiers joined the Jesuits on 6 June 1666 and distinguished himself in the careers of teaching and preaching. He took the order of priesthood and exercised the holy ministry. In 1689 he left the Jesuits to join the unreformed Cluny order. A writer and essayist, he composed or printed most of the works that came from his pen. Boileau mentions the Abbé de Villiers in his poetry, and calls him "the Matamore of Cluny", "because he had a bold air and imperious speech". He never put his name to his works.
=500  \\$aDigitalisation of later edition of 1753: https://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k5531143f.texteImage

=500  \\$aHenriette-Julie de Murat was an aristocratic French writer of the late 17th century.
=500  \\$aIn 1697 she published Memoirs of the Countess of M***, a two-volume collection of false "memoirs" which was meant as a response to Charles de Saint-Évremond's 1696 book Memoirs of the Life of Count D*** before his Retirement, which had portrayed women as incapable of virtue and fickle. Murat's book was successful and was even translated into English.

=500  \\$aLe Misant(h)rope was a Dutch journal originally published every monday from May 19th 1711 tot December 26th 1712 . Published in 2 vols. in The Hague by T.Johnson in 1711 and 1712. The magazine was reprinted in 1726 (own revision by Van Effen) in The Hague; 1741 (Lausanne/Geneva) and twice in 1742 (Amsterdam and The Hague).
=500  \\$aJustus van Effen was a Dutch author, who wrote chiefly in French but also made crucial contributions to Dutch literature. A journalist, he imitated The Spectator with the publication of the Dutch-language Hollandsche Spectator. He gained international fame as a writer of French periodicals and a translator from English into French, and he is also recognized as one of the most important Dutch language writers of the 18th century and an influential figure of the Dutch Enlightenment
=500  \\$aOften considered as one of the best essayistic texts from the early Enlightenment.
=500  \\$aFrontispiece vol.1 is an engraved portrait of the author by Pieter Tanjé (1706-1761)  after des Angeles (1716-1761)

=100  \\$aEffen, Justus van$d1684-1735$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2574405$98518
=245  \\$aLa Bagatelle, $bou Discours ironiques$n1-2/2
=250  \\$arev. ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bUytwerf$c1742
=300  \\$a2 vols ([xxvi]-300-[8] + 289-[9] pages)$btitle pages in red and black ink
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=490  \\$aOeuvres diverses de Mr. Juste van Effen$v3-4/4
=500  \\$aMoral observations in a satirical tone. Interests: fashion, religion, morals. Authors studied: Addison, Swift, La Bruyère.
=500  \\$aDutch Journal published every thursday and monday between 5 mai 1718 and 13 avril 1719. 
=500  \\$aAlready the author of several journals including the first spectator in French (Le Misanthrope), Justus van Effen attempted to capture the Regency spirit in France with La Bagatelle. Produced as a twice-weekly quarter sheet, La Bagatelle included witty observations on contemporary society, literary controversies, bolder, more subversive reflections on questions of religion, as well as short works of poetry and prose. 
=500  \\$aSince 1718, the publication of the Literary Journal had been delayed by the nonchalance of the bookseller Johnson. For van Effen this meant a considerable loss of money, so he sought some compensation. He launched La Bagatelle for personal reasons.
=500  \\$aThe author intended (cf. Preface) to lead men from the ridiculousness of custom and fashion to Reason; but his ironic style was not understood. Convinced of his error, he wanted to change his plan: "I will put a capital I on the frontispiece of my Feuille Volante, so that the public will be aware of it" (I, as in Irony), he declares at the end of the first volume. In fact, van Effen himself, a serious man, found it difficult to sustain the satirical tone. In short, La Bagatelle was not a success.
=500  \\$aPreface in the issue of Monday 5 September 1718: "to bring Men back from the ridiculous impressions of Custom and Fashion to the eternal and invariable principles of Reason, which must be the only Rule of our Conduct".
=504  \\$aevery volume contains an index
=504  \\$aEdited by James L. Schorr (ed.), ‘La Bagatelle’ (1718-1719): a critical edition of Justus van Effen’s journal, in  'Oxford University Studies in the Enlightenment', November 2014. ISBN 9780729411493, 352 pages,
=590  \\$aOù l'on prête des Sophismes ingénieux au Vice & à l'Extravagance, pour en faire mieux sentir le ridicule. Par Mr. van Effen, Docteur en Droit, & Membre de la Société Royale de Londres

=100  \\$aDrouaux, Étienne$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q28494512$98519
=245  \\$aMéthode nouvelle pour apprendre le plain-chant$bDivise en quatre parties

=300  \\$a[viii]-144 pages$bmusical examples
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1672 Paris by Robert & Ballard
=500  \\$aÉtienne Drouaux was a musician and composer active in Paris in the last third of the 17th century.
=500  \\$aDrouaux is best known as the author of a method of plainsong which enjoyed a certain success, since about ten editions were published between 1672 and 1705. This method was part of a wave of publications of new methods which tended to give a somewhat secure basis to the practice of plainchant. But it appears that Drouaux was largely inspired by Jean Millet's method of 1666, keeping the most practical elements and eliminating the old authorities that encumbered it.
=500  \\$aDrouaux' first name is really Étienne (or Estienne), not Henri Blaise, as Fétis or Ton thought

=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aVerona$bTumermani$c1728
=300  \\$a[12]-348-[12] pages, 14 inserted folded pages with plates$bbound in white vellum, illustrations, engraved title page
=500  \\$aMaffei was a Venetian writer and art critic, author of many articles and plays. An antiquarian with a humanist education whose publications on Etruscan antiquities stand as incunables of Etruscology. Founder of the Lapidary Museum of Verona. A multifaceted figure in the Italian and European panorama. Military, philosopher, poet, playwright, historian, scientist, opera librettist, but above all a passionate fanatic of antiquities. He was an avid collector of ancient manuscripts and epigraphs, which he acquired in Verona, Italy or brought from all over the Mediterranean basin thanks to the possessions of the Republic of Venice, of which Verona was a part. Maffei was a prominent member of the Veronese Accademia Filarmonica and he worked for the realization of the theater that would be inaugurated in 1732 with Vivaldi's 'La fida ninfa', for which he wrote the libretto.

=041  \\$alat
=100  \\$aMaggi, Girolamo$dc. 1523-1572$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q5564769$98540
=245  \\$aDe equuleo
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bFrisius$c1664
=300  \\$a[xxx]-196-[14] pages$bbound in white vellum, engraved title page, illustrations, 1 inserted folded page$c7x13 cm
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aTreatise on torture devices written in 1571, first published posthumously 1609.
=500  \\$aMaggi was an Italian scholar, jurist, poet, military engineer, urban planner, philologist, archaeologist, mathematician, and naturalist who studied at Bologna under Francis Robortello. He authored several works, including a collection of poems on the Flemish wars, and several on the subject of philosophy.
=500  \\$aMaggi was a judge and military defense engineer in Famagusta on Cyprus when the island was invaded by Ottoman Turks in 1571. Besieged by the Turks, he invented machines to defend Famagusta against their attacks. When the island was conquered, Maggi was sent to the dungeons at Constantinople where, locked in chains, he wrote from memory two detailed treatises, De tintinnabulis, on bells and carillons, and the explicitly illustrated De equuleo, on torture devices.In attempts to be freed, he dedicated the first treatise to Carolus Rym (Charles Ramire), ambassador to the Holy Roman Emperor Maximilian II, and the second treatise to François de Noailles, bishop of Aire and ambassador to the King of France. They were pleased with his works, and endeavoured to obtain his release. Their efforts, however, were brought to light as he was being released to the Italian ambassador. The prison captain ordered him to be detained and executed by strangulation. His two treatises were published posthumously in 1608 and 1609, respectively.

=500  \\$aTreatise on (the use of) bells and carillons, written in 1571, first published posthumously 1608
=500  \\$aMaggi was an Italian scholar, jurist, poet, military engineer, urban planner, philologist, archaeologist, mathematician, and naturalist who studied at Bologna under Francis Robortello. He authored several works, including a collection of poems on the Flemish wars, and several on the subject of philosophy.

=500  \\$aMaggi was a judge and military defense engineer in Famagusta on Cyprus when the island was invaded by Ottoman Turks in 1571. Besieged by the Turks, he invented machines to defend Famagusta against their attacks. When the island was conquered, Maggi was sent to the dungeons at Constantinople where, locked in chains, he wrote from memory two detailed treatises, De tintinnabulis, on bells and carillons, and the explicitly illustrated De equuleo, on torture devices.In attempts to be freed, he dedicated the first treatise to Carolus Rym (Charles Ramire), ambassador to the Holy Roman Emperor Maximilian II, and the second treatise to François de Noailles, bishop of Aire and ambassador to the King of France. They were pleased with his works, and endeavoured to obtain his release. Their efforts, however, were brought to light as he was being released to the Italian ambassador. The prison captain ordered him to be detained and executed by strangulation. His two treatises were published posthumously in 1608 and 1609, respectively.

=100  \\$aHolberg, Ludvig$d1684-1754$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q216692$98546
=245  \\$aPeter Paars$bein comisches Heldengedicht
=250  \\$a1st ed.

=300  \\$a[lxviii]-420 pages$b14 inserted engraved plates, engraved title pages and frontispiece
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aTitle page has emblem "In Spe et Labore"
=500  \\$aPeder Paars is a comic-epic poem that appeared in four parts in the years 1719-20 under the pseudonym of Hans Michelsen. The poem is a parody of the heroic epics of antiquity and Renaissance. Holberg particularly alludes to Vergil's great Roman epic Aeneid.
=500  \\$aThe poem enjoyed great success, but the description of conditions on Anholt prompted the then owner, Frederik Rostgaard, to complain to the king, demanding that the book be burned by the executioner. The king nevertheless decided that the writing - although it "could rather have been omitted than written" - could be accepted, as it was a "fictitious sketch." 
=500  \\$aHolberg was a writer, essayist, philosopher, historian and playwright born in Bergen, Norway, during the time of the Dano-Norwegian dual monarchy. He was influenced by Humanism, the Enlightenment and the Baroque. Holberg is considered the founder of modern Danish and Norwegian literature. He is best known for the comedies he wrote in 1722–1723 for the Lille Grønnegade Theatre in Copenhagen.
=500  \\$aPaars was a breakthrough in Holberg's writing in the direction of satire and the many comedies for which he is still known.
=500  \\$aThe composer J.A. Scheibe translated Peder Paars into German. In 1740 he became kapellmeister at the court of the danisch king Christian IV, and remained in Denmark until his death. He had a very sharp pen, evident in his satirical writings or political pamphlets,  but also in the first biography of his friend Baron Ludvig Holberg, The biography not only provides information on Holberg but also indirectly on Scheibe.
=504  \\$aPaars and his crew discover that the inhabitants of Anholt, who "live Christianly and feed on debris", are plundering and robbing the castaways. The rest of the island is watching the commoners who live in the blackest superstition. The bailiff passes judgement in his own favour, while the priest relies on old Catholic sermons.

=024  \\$2Wikidata$aQ3320970
=041  \\$alat$hlat
=245  \\$aMonita secreta of de geheime instructiën die door de Jesuieten in stilte worden nageleefd
=260  \\$aOostburg$bBronswijk$c1868
=300  \\$a56 pages
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aAnti-Jesuit pamphlet
=500  \\$aThe Monita secreta ("Secret Instructions") is an anonymous document from 1614 whose original title is Monita privata Societatis Iesu . This booklet gives instructions to the Jesuits on how to proceed in order to gain power and wealth. It is a fake - and known as such since 1615 - but it had great success with the enemies of the Jesuits, including the 19th and 20th centuries.  Scholars regard the document as an anti-Jesuit forgery, written by Hieronymus Zahorowski, a Jesuit dismissed from the Order.
=520  \\$aAccording to the Monita, Jesuits are to use every means at their disposal to acquire wealth for the order. For instance, Jesuits are encouraged to entice promising young men to enter the order and endow it with their estates; rich widows are to be cajoled and dissuaded from remarriage. Every means is to be used for the advancement of Jesuits to bishoprics or other ecclesiastical dignities and to discredit the members of other orders, while the world is to be persuaded that the Society is animated by the purest and least interested motives: the reputation of those who quit it is to be assailed and maligned in every way.

=059  \\$av
=245  \\$aLes Psaumes de David, mis en vers françois, & les cantiques sacrés
=250  \\$aRev. ed.
=260  \\$aBasel$bImhof$c1774
=300  \\$a472-180 pages$bgilded edges
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aIncluding one loose page with ms. notes about psalmbooks, probably written by D.W.L. Milo, on the backside of a concert flyer.
=500  \\$aThe translation of the psalms go back to John Calvin (1509-1564). In 1562 a collection of psalms (known as the Genevan Psalms) was published, suitable to be sung during the service. Calvin had started rhyming in Strasbourg himself. Back in Geneva, he handed this work over to Clément Marot and Beza, while he asked Guillaume Franc, Louis Bourgeois and Maitre Pierre to compose the music. Calvin's zeal in making a collection of psalms arose from his wish to use the Bible alone, also for the hymn. Later editions were edited by members of the 'Compagnie des pasteurs de l'église protestante de Genève'. 
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1698
=561  \\$aEx libris D.W.L. Milo (stamp)

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aDorat, Claude-Joseph$d1734-1780$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q361456$98577
=245  \\$aLes Prôneurs, ou Le Tartuffe littéraire,$bComédie en trois actes, en vers.
=260  \\$aParis$bDelalain$c1777
=300  \\$aviii-87 pages$b4 insterted engravings
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aA lively satire of the people in Julie de Lespinasse's society, i.e. the philosophical party. Dorat kept it in his portfolio for several years without being able to have it performed. The philosophers, who were not spared, used the powerful men of their party to prevent the play from being performed. The main character of the play is D'Alembert who, under the name of "Callidès", plays the role of leader of the advocates. The scene in which he initiates a young follower into the mysteries of the order is very pleasant. In this play we find some portraits drawn with a rather vigorous brush, among others, those of Palissot and Clément de Dijon, of whom Dorat had reason to complain; of the former, because he had portrayed him in a less than advantageous manner in his Dunciade; of the latter, because he had made a bitter criticism of his poem De la déclamation.
=500  \\$amotto by Voltaire on the frontispiece: "Le Philosophe est seul, & l'Imposteur fait Secte."
=500  \\$aDorat published most of his works with numerous engravings by Clément-Pierre Marillier and Charles Eisen, which made them masterpieces of art and typographic luxury
=500  \\$a4 beautiful engravings after Clément-Pierre Marillier (1740-1808), by Pierre Duffos le Jeune (1742-1816) , Louis Michel Halbou (1730-1809) and Pierre Adrien Le Beau (1744-1804)
=561  \\$aEx libris of Bibl. Kammer , Stockholm (plate), Ida Schoeller (plate) and H. Volkmann 1926 (manuscript)

=100  \\$aVolkmann, Johann Jacob$d1732-1803$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q113563$98583
=245  \\$aHistorisch-kritische Nachrichten von Italien $p1-3/3
=260  \\$aLeipzig$bFritsch$c1770-1
=300  \\$a3 vols. (xxvi-682-[8] + viii-872 + [viii]-846-[42] pages)$bengraved frontispiece, red edges, engraved title vignet
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aOne of the most influential German art books of the 18th century. Spread over three volumes, it systematically provides information about churches, palaces, art collections, musical life, but also about the history of all important Italian cities from Turin to Naples. As a guide to historical Italy, the 'Volkmann' accompanied Goethe, Karl Philipp Moritz, Johann Gottfried Seume and many other Germans on their travels. Goethe, for example, wrote to Charlotte von Stein in 1787: " I am now reading the good, dry Volckmanns zweyten Theil to note what I have not yet seen." (Kippenberg)
=500  \\$a3 identical engraved title vignets depicting 2 little boys holding a map of Italy
=500  \\$aFrontispiece engraving by Christian Gottlieb Geyser (1742-1803)
=500  \\$amanuscript notes on front matter of vol. 1 and 2
=500  \\$apensil markings throughout
=561  \\$aEx libris Riegel- und Wiesnersche Lesebibliothek Nürnberg (plate)

Aus den neuesten französischen und englischen Reisebeschreibungen und aus eignen Anmerkungen zusammengetragen.

=500  \\$aJohan Georg Hamann was a German librettist and writer, a cousin of his famous nephew of the same name J. G. Hamann (1730-1788). He became a private tutor and was active as a publicist, contributing to Gottsched's periodical 'Die vernünftigen Tadlerinnen'. 
=500  \\$aHe wrote for Georg Philipp Telemann: the libretto to the opera 'Margaretha, Queen of Castile' (Hamburg 1730), translated Metastasio's recitatives of  Didone abbandonata for 'Der Streit der kindlichen Pflicht, oder, Die Flucht des Aeneas nach Latien' (Hamburg 1731), and the libretto for the opera 'Der Weiseste in Sidon' (Hamburg 1733).
=590  \\$aNebst einer kurtzen Erklärung der mythologischen Nahmen, aus den besten und neuesten deutschen Dichtern zusammen getragen, und der studirenden Jugend zum bequemen Gebrauch an statt eines Poetischen Lexici, mit einer Anweisung zur reinen und wahren Deutschen Dicht-Kunst ans Licht gestellet.

=245  \\$aAdres-Calender der Königl. Preußl. Haupt- und Residentz-Städte Berlin
=260  \\$aBerlin$bKöniglichen Preußischen Academie der Wissenschaften$c1764
=300  \\$a[xxviii]-247-[42] pages$btitle page in red and black ink
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aadress book of Berlin in 1764
=500  \\$aThe Berlin address calendars appeared annually between 1704 and 1918 under different titles.
=500  \\$aThe Berlin address calendars list the higher-ranking persons and office holders of the royal Prussian residential cities of Berlin and Potsdam as well as their authorities, administrations and organizations. The address and description of the authorities are listed, as well as the person's name, official title and private address. At the end of each entry is an index of names. From 1878 onwards, information from the neighboring city of Charlottenburg is also included.

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aChoffin, David Étienne$d1703-1773$4aut$98590
=245  \\$aAmusemens philologiques en prose et en vers$bou mélange agréable de diverses pièces, concernant l'histoire des personnes célèbres, les évènemens mémorables & l'histoire naturelle$p3
=260  \\$aHalle$bMaison des Orphelins$c1780
=300  \\$a[xxx]-397 pages$bengraved frontispiece, title page in red and black ink, title page engraved with editor's emblem
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aLater edition
=500  \\$aoriginal in 2 vols. , 1749-1750
=500  \\$aChoffin was a scholar and philologist, born in Héricourt (F) on October 2, 1703, died in Halle (D) in January 1773.  He obtained the double position of professor of modern languages at the school of the Orphans and at the university of Halle, and he contributed by his writings and his lessons to spread the use of French in Saxony.
=500  \\$aEditor's emblem depicting sunbeams & cultivated land with saying "illo splendete levabor' and the initials WH, referring to Weisenhaus Halle  (La Maison des Orphelins à Halle). The Latin motto "Illo splendente levabor" (By his splendor I will be exalted) was intended to testify to the godliness of the institution. The sower in the foreground was interpreted by Bible-loving contemporaries as a reference to the Gospel of Mark (4:14): "The sower sows the word." And this was precisely Francke's basic concern: to change the world by means of the word.
=500  \\$aIntresting frontispiece engraving, depicting Germany, rulers' portraits and battlefields, with inscription "Teutschland hofft der Friedens Zeit - L'Allemagne attend le tems de la paix".
=501  \\$aBound in with ‘Dictionnaire abrégé de la fable ou de la mythologie’

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aGodeau, Antoine$d1605-1672$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q586272$97907
=245  \\$aPoësies chrestiennes
=250  \\$a2nd ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bPetit$c1660
=300  \\$a508 pages$bengraved title page
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aAntoine Godeau was a French bishop, poet and exegete.
=500  \\$aAntoine Godeau (1605-1672) first published the Poësies Chrestiennes in 1633 in the context of the Catholic Reformation which encouraged spiritual revival. This lyric collection is emblematic of his comprehensive poetic and spiritual work. Godeau became the Bishop of Grasse in 1636 and devoted his poetic gifts to enlightening the readers. This new edition is the latest version of the Poësies Chrestiennes (1660), which is pastoral Catholic verse addressed to the socialites of the time. The versatile poet expressed himself in various forms, registers and topics to convey the Christian dogma and the Bible. The content and the purpose of the book fluctuated. The Poësies chrestiennes was thus a field for experimentation : it became Antoine Godeau's laboratory for all his pastoral and lyric work. The poet defined the principles of a poetry which was based on the conciliation of divine enthusiasm and reason, a poetry where grace and beauty met. The paraphrase of the Scriptures was an opportunity to explore the conciliation of Parnassus and Calvary, as well as the specificity of a classical poetic language in the making, endowing it with gentleness and clarity. Poetry appeared to be the ideal way to instill Christian truths in the heart of the faithful. The religious conversion of secular literary rhetoric prepared the layman to hear the poet-preacher’s vigorous speech. Antoine Godeau tempered his Augustinian anthropology by promoting a life both wordly and pious, in chime with the ideal of Christian “honnêteté”. The poet spiritualized profane aesthetics, which showed his unrelenting desire to adapt his conversion discourse to a public eager to be edified by the “delectare”.
=504  \\$aCamille Venner, Édition critique des "Poësies chrestiennes" (1660) d'Antoine Godeau précédée d'une introduction sur la pastorale lyrique et catholique de cet auteur, These, Université de Lorraine, 2018
https://hal.univ-lorraine.fr/tel-01752385

=100  \\$aSaavedra Fajardo, Diego de$d1584-1648$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2715411$98592
=245  \\$aIdea de un principe politico christiano, representada en cien empresas
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bJanssonius$c1664
=300  \\$a[xxxv]-983 pages
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aDiego de Saavedra Fajardo (1584-1648) was a Spanish diplomat and man of letters.

=500  \\$ain 1640 Saavedra published the anti-Machiavellian emblem book Empresas Políticas. Idea de un príncipe político cristiano, a hundred short essays about the education of a prince. This work was written primarily for the son of King Philip IV. It passed through a number of editions and was translated in several languages.
=500  \\$aSaavedra's 'Idea de un príncipe político cristiano' was a very erudite work that uses the literary sort of emblem, put by Andrea Alciato with his 'Emblemata' translated in 1549 and that has a mainly moral and philosophical character. His work, however, was mainly inspired by the 'Emblemata política' (1618), by Jakob Bruck Angermunt, being the intention of the author to compose a guide for the suitable political formation of a Christian prince.

=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aMoritz von Strachwitz (1822-1847) was a German lyric poet. When traveling in Italy in 1847 he was taken ill in Venice, and died in Vienna. Although he had thus only reached his twenty-fifth year, he revealed a lyric genius of remarkable force and originality. His early death was a great loss to German letters; for he was by far the most promising of the younger lyric poets of his time.

=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1743
=590  \\$aWorinn enthalten: Die Evolutions zu Pferde und zu Fuß, das Manual und die Chargirung, und wie der Dienst im Felde und in der Garnison geschehen soll. Auch wornach die sämtlichen Officiers sich zur verhalten haben. Desgleichen wie viel an Tractament bezahlet und davon abgezogen wird, auch wie die Mondirung gemacht werden soll. Ordnung halber in IX. Theile, ein jeder Theil in gewisse Tituls, und ein jeder Titul in gewisse Articuls abgefasset.
